  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e1dce3e8-60ed-4527-a16f-438fd6184faa'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9244169601824753937">Tessa has everything to lose. Hardin has nothing to lose… except her. <br/><br/>After a tumultuous beginning to their relationship, Tessa and Hardin were on the path to making things work.   <span id="freeText9244169601824753937" style="display:none">Tessa has everything to lose. Hardin has nothing to lose… except her. <br /><br />After a tumultuous beginning to their relationship, Tessa and Hardin were on the path to making things work. Tessa knew Hardin could be cruel, but when a bombshell revelation is dropped about the origins of their relationship—and Hardin’s mysterious past—Tessa is beside herself.<br /><br />Hardin will always be… Hardin. But is he really the deep, thoughtful guy Tessa fell madly in love with despite his angry exterior—or has he been a stranger all along? She wishes she could walk away. It’s just not that easy. Not with the memory of passionate nights spent in his arms. His electric touch. His hungry kisses.<br /><br />Still, Tessa’s not sure she can endure one more broken promise. She put so much on hold for Hardin—school, friends, her mom, a relationship with a guy who really loved her, and now possibly even a promising new career. She needs to move forward with her life.<br /><br />Hardin knows he made a mistake, possibly the biggest one of his life. He’s not going down without a fight. But can he change? <i>Will</i> he change for love?<br /><br />Book Two of the After series—now newly revised and expanded, Anna Todd’s After fan-fiction racked up 1 billion reads online and captivated readers across the globe. Experience the Internet’s most talked-about book for yourself!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9244169601824753937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/96826504-tasneem-h"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1598392336i/96826504._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/96826504-tasneem-h">☾ Tasneem H. ☽</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Ok, so I'm 13, and judging from the reviews on Goodreads and rants on youtube, it isn't very appropriate as it has sex scenes, a character giving thei<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Ok, so I'm 13, and judging from the reviews on Goodreads and rants on youtube, it isn't very appropriate as it has sex scenes, a character giving their partner a blowjob, physical and mental abuse, violence, and overall the relationship in the book is INCREDIBLY toxic. It honestly depends if your 11-year-old can handle it and is mature enough to understand what's going on in the book. There are way better romance, YA, and Wattpad books out there with greater quality (and with greater writing and grammar). Don't let your kid (who's now 12) waste their time and get an awful representation of a young, "healthy" relationship. There are better options out there and I hope they don't read this garbage of a book and fanfiction.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1286081685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1286081685" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286081685?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286081685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15928811466105985892">I don't think I can reiterate enough how much I hate this series... "But Angela why the high rating?"... Well let me break it down for you, this is the best worst thing I've ever read. It's so addictive it's insane. It's like the potato chip bag of books. You don't want to eat more than a handful but somehow wind up eating the whole bag.<br/><br/><i>After We Collided</i> is seriously just the book <i>After </i>again. It's the same shit different day. Tessa and Hardin continue their on again off again, I hate you but ca</span>
  <span id="freeText15928811466105985892" style="display:none">I don't think I can reiterate enough how much I hate this series... "But Angela why the high rating?"... Well let me break it down for you, this is the best worst thing I've ever read. It's so addictive it's insane. It's like the potato chip bag of books. You don't want to eat more than a handful but somehow wind up eating the whole bag.<br><br><i>After We Collided</i> is seriously just the book <i>After </i>again. It's the same shit different day. Tessa and Hardin continue their on again off again, I hate you but can't live without you bull that they did in the first. Tessa is still the same up tight-jump to conclusion- why is she dating this guy- train wreck that she was in the first. Hardin is the same glass smashing-must fight anything with a pulse-emotional flip flopping dbag he was in the first as well. Tessa continues to say one thing then do another. Hardin continues to come up with white pointless lies for again, no reason. To give Todd some credit she did give her characters a little more development and personality in this one than the first. Tessa managed to have a little more spine than a jellyfish and Hardin was a lot more comical than in the first.<br><br><b><i>"Just because he can't love you the way you want him to doesn't mean he doesn't love you with everything he has."</i></b><br><br>As far as the plot line goes <i>AWC</i> is like I said above, just <i>After </i>only written in dual Pov between Hardin and Tessa. A lot of people are saying how important this was because we get to see what's going on in both our leads heads... Hate to be the bearer of bad news but there is nothing of substance going on in either of their brains. 95% of the time you'll be screaming "<i>wow if these two just actually chilled the F out and had a real conversation this book would be 200 pages shorter and sweeter</i>." This book is a cluster of what the heck am I reading moments. That being said I did enjoy the dual views. The plot is as delicious as soggy bread an at this point in time you're probably still wondering why I've given it such high marks... Well because again Todd has managed to hook me in. Every time I set this book down within minutes I had to pick it back up. The combination of perfectly placed twist, smutty goodness, my hatred of characters, and stupid plot must have fried all my braincells and in return made me love this story.<i> The After Series</i> brings nothing new or original to the ya/na genre. The moment it pulled the 50 shades of gross it took everything in me not to set this book on fire (if you've read it you know EXACTLY what I'm talking about). Though the characters are awful and the plot is weak all the twist made up for it. Because when those twist happen... Well lets just say my situation looked a little like this:<br><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-uugWBV9l1hs/VW-T8SStI9I/AAAAAAAABxg/0iQtvg_DoCg/s1600/after%2Bwe.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433376499ra/15090548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>Both took me completely by surprise. Also the smut in this book is so on point! Haters go ahead and hate, don't care, I ate it up! <br><br><b>
  <i>After We Collided </i>had me so mad, so angry, so annoyed, and so so entertained. It's a story about a toxic relationship between an idiot drunk, controlling, cocky dick weed and a naive, pathetic, stupid, co-dependent moody girl, and yet I can't seem to get enough.
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15928811466105985892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2059423797" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2059423797" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2059423797?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22473458-after-we-collided">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059423797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3478936631942417244">After finishing the first book in the 'After' series, I immediately jumped into this second book. There was no way that I was going to quit this series with the way things ended at the end of 'After'--absolutely, no way! I had to know how things were going to play out for this disastrous couple. They are like crack! It might kill me. I know it's really not healthy...but I just can't seem to pull myself away from it!<br/><br/>If I thought that Hardin and Tessa were going to grow up and start treating each </span>
  <span id="freeText3478936631942417244" style="display:none">After finishing the first book in the 'After' series, I immediately jumped into this second book. There was no way that I was going to quit this series with the way things ended at the end of 'After'--absolutely, no way! I had to know how things were going to play out for this disastrous couple. They are like crack! It might kill me. I know it's really not healthy...but I just can't seem to pull myself away from it!<br /><br />If I thought that Hardin and Tessa were going to grow up and start treating each other better, I would've been sorely disappointed. These two are every bit as toxic as they were the first time around. The back and forth, break-up and make-up, abusive cycle continues, strong as ever. Of course, I'm such a glutton for punishment that I had to have a front row seat for all of it!<br /><br />Picking up right where the first book ended, Tessa does her best to try and piece her life back together. She has been betrayed by everyone that she thought were her friends -- most of all, Hardin. Unfortunately, the manipulative jackass succeeded in tying her to him when he tricked her into moving into an apartment with him and away from the dorms. This will make distancing herself from him more difficult than she had hoped.<br /><br />While Tessa makes a weak attempt at moving on, Hardin sets out to prove that his feelings for her are genuine. Of course, every time he starts to make any progress in that regard he does something that sabotages all of his efforts. They truly are their own worst enemies.<br /><br />For what it's worth, Hardin does seem to show some actual emotions in this book. Mainly, his regret and heartache shines through. It's hard to feel sorry for him though, since all of his pain is entirely the result of his own cruel actions. To make matters worse, every time he starts to gain a little "nice guy" stock, he goes and does something abhorrent again, reminding me of what a despicable asshat he is. Some big revelations about his past only further prove that he is not to be trusted. He really is deplorable...but I love to hate him!<br /><br />I also found myself feeling a little more irritated with Tessa's weakness this time around. Can you say "doormat"? How many times is this girl going to fall for his crap? She also played the same childish games over and over, using other guys to make Hardin jealous, only to play the victim when she got the reaction she was looking for all along. <br /><br />I felt sorry for Tessa at first. By the end of this book, I was marveling at the fact that she hadn't been weeded out as part of the process of natural selection. Surely, this girl is too stupid to live!<br /><br />That being said, I still can't pull myself away from this angsty, infuriating story. It is like watching a trashy talk show or soap opera. It's unrealistic. The relationships are toxic. It probably kills off brain cells. However, I can't get enough of it. It is my latest guilty pleasure. I'm kind of ashamed to admit it, but I'm completely hooked on this series.<br /><br />Like the first book, 'After We Collided' ends with a huge cliffhanger. Anna Todd certainly knows how to pull me back in. At this point, I think my relationship with this series is much like the relationship between Hardin and Tessa. I should probably cut all ties and get out while I can, but I just can't seem to resist the pull. I'm on to the third book in this addictive, dysfunctional romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3478936631942417244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5800217081452638013" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496839308i/22957132._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496589189ra/22930926.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496436563ra/22912872.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496515529ra/22922651.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496589026ra/22930904.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️! After We Collided, book 2 of 5. The tumultuous against-all-odds romance between tatted rebel Hardin Scott &amp; good girl Tessa Young!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Just because he can’t love you the way you want him to doesn’t mean he doesn’t love you with everything he has…”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><u>Books in The After series should be read in order:</u><br><b>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090449623" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952340915" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Collided</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994022284" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Fell</a><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000467437" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After Ever Happy</a><br>Book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000467456" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Before</a></b><br><br>The After series is the epic love saga between flawed rebel bad boy student and editor <b>Hardin Allen Scott</b> and naïve good girl student and intern editor <b>Theresa Lynn Young, Tessa.</b><br><br><i>In <b>After, book 1</b> Tessa met Hardin and an <b>unlikely friendship</b> blossomed into more only to be shattered by secrets, jealousy and betrayal.</i><br><br><b>After We Collided, book 2</b> will test their relationship taking their connection to another level.; A <b>dysfunctional and co-dependent</b> love with their biggest obstacles to overcome from within. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496016874ra/22874859.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Nine words to describe <b> Hardin Allen Scott:</b> Unpredictable, moody, flawed, broken, aloof, secretive, demanding, conflicted and possessive.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496016874ra/22874860.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Nine words to describe <b> Theresa Lynn Young, Tessa:</b> Organized, meek, compulsive, goal-oriented, determined, naïve, trusting, curious and forgiving.<br><br><b>After We Collided,</b> told from dual POVs, is an <b>all-consuming, addicting,</b> at times angsty journey of <b>self-discovery, testing boundaries, pushing limits</b> and <b>surrendering</b> it all for love. It ends opening another chapter, leading right to book 3, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994022284" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Fell</a>
</b> for the <b>continuation</b> of their journey.<br><br>***<br>Hero: ★★★★★<br>Heroine: ★★★★<br>Plot: ★★★★★<br>Storytelling: ★★★★★<br>Sexual tension: ★★★★★<br>Sex scenes: ★★★★★<br>Story ending: N/A<br>******************************************<br><b>OVERALL RATING:</b> ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Angst: <b>| HIGH FOCUS |</b><br>Darkness: <b>| MEDIUM FOCUS |</b><br>Humor: <b>| LOW FOCUS |</b><br>Kink: <b>| LOW FOCUS |</b><br>Romance: <b>| HIGH FOCUS |</b><br>Sex frequency: <b>| MEDIUM FOCUS |</b><br>Suspense: <b>| MEDIUM FOCUS |</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496839308ra/22957133.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495396964ra/22813189.gif" width="81" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496589189ra/22930926.gif" width="81" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495397142ra/22813203.gif" width="81" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495397230ra/22813206.gif" width="81" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495397307ra/22813208.gif" width="81" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5800217081452638013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13284964151183067373">A GUIDE FOR ABUSE, SEXISM AND TOXIC RELATIONSHIPS. <br/><br/><b>These books romanticize an abusive relationship, which horrifies me.</b> It is basically a step by step manual to emotional abuse and toxic behavior.<br/><br/>Here are some of the most common sings to identify an abusive relationship, according to experts:<br/>Whirlwind Romance<br/>Control/Dominance<br/>Rage Episodes <br/>Isolating you from friends and family. <br/>Extreme and Unreasonable Jealousy <br/>Refusing to communicate.<br/>Withdrawal of affection. <br/>Double Standards <br/>Idealization/Devalua</span>
  <span id="freeText13284964151183067373" style="display:none">A GUIDE FOR ABUSE, SEXISM AND TOXIC RELATIONSHIPS. <br /><br /><b>These books romanticize an abusive relationship, which horrifies me.</b> It is basically a step by step manual to emotional abuse and toxic behavior.<br /><br />Here are some of the most common sings to identify an abusive relationship, according to experts:<br />Whirlwind Romance<br />Control/Dominance<br />Rage Episodes <br />Isolating you from friends and family. <br />Extreme and Unreasonable Jealousy <br />Refusing to communicate.<br />Withdrawal of affection. <br />Double Standards <br />Idealization/Devaluation<br />Lack of Accountability<br />Verbal Abuse<br />Humiliating or embarrassing you.<br />Ignoring or excluding you. <br />Emotional Blackmail <br />Extreme moodiness. <br />Financial control. <br /><br /><b>This “romance” covers EVERY. SINGLE. ONE. of them. The male character in this series, Harden, exhibits all of them, repeatedly, towards Tessa.</b> It horrifies me that this can pass as a romantic book. I worry about every single person that might be influenced by this and think it is ok, romantic or even desirable. <b>The relationship between this characters is an unacceptable one, and it should only be an example of HOW NOT TO be, WHAT NOT TO do. </b><br /><br /><b>APPALING</b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322612232?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/41817199-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789113065038" href="/book/show/26823295-n-r-vi-tvekade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41817199-alex?shelf=painfully-bad">painfully-bad</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322612232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8721314586125842073">I wasn't planning on reviewing this book. <br/>But then I heard that they are making a movie/ series(?) out of this shitshow. <br/><br/>The After series was written as Harry Styles fanfiction on Wattpad. I gained a lot of attention and was later rewritten into a novell. This is nothing new, we have seen it before. I have nothing against fanfiction, it's playful and fun but it's not supposed to be taken seriously and this book is trying sooo hard to be taken seriously. <br/><br/>This book as about the "princess girl" Tes</span>
  <span id="freeText8721314586125842073" style="display:none">I wasn't planning on reviewing this book. <br />But then I heard that they are making a movie/ series(?) out of this shitshow. <br /><br />The After series was written as Harry Styles fanfiction on Wattpad. I gained a lot of attention and was later rewritten into a novell. This is nothing new, we have seen it before. I have nothing against fanfiction, it's playful and fun but it's not supposed to be taken seriously and this book is trying sooo hard to be taken seriously. <br /><br />This book as about the "princess girl" Tessa and the "bad boy" Hardin and their "love story". The book is filled with drama, sex, fighting and even different types of abuse. Now, heres the thing with YA; it can have the worst set of characters and worts storyline ever and the language can be plain and mediocre, but if the books is smacked with sex and flowing body fluids, it will sell.It doesn't matter how harmful the book actually is because people will bite right into it as long it's full of spiraling hormones and this feels like a trend in modern YA? <br /><br />When you hear about a fanfiction piece turn't movie I'm pretty sure that your thoughts goes straight to Fifty Shades of Grey. For those who don't know: Fifty Shades is fanfiction based of the Twilight Saga, a completely fictional piece of work. I did have problems with Fifty Shades and I do have major problems with the After series. <br /> 1. Fifty Shades is an <b>Adult</b> book whilst After is a marketed towards <b>Young Adults</b> aka "Kids" but both are extremely abusive and dark erotica. <br /> 2. Fifty Shades, though fan fiction, was based on a completely fictional, "original" work whilst After is inspired by A REAL, BREATHING HUMAN BEEING THAT ACTUALLY EXISTS. Doesn't that make anyone else uncomfortable? Anna Todd sat at home, infront of her computer, franticly writing out her sloppy, wet fantasies about Harry Styles and then posting it to Wattpad..? I can't be the only one who get's weirded out about that? <br /> 3. The books aren't even good? They have NO storyline. <i>Girls is picked on by boy. Boy advances on girl anyway. Girl is "confused". Girls and boy have sex. Repeat... Repeat...</i> It's just sex, alcohol, drugs and abuse over and over. Not to mention that Anna Todd's language is terrible.<br /> 4. A producer saw the numbers these books are getting and saw a chance at a fat paycheck. I bet they didn't even read the books. <br /><br />I shouldn't let it make me this upset but it bothers me that young people are going to read these and see the movie and make up a picture in their heads that this is okay. A relationship is supposed to be fun and uplifting! Not filled with drama and emotional abuse! <br /> We are in an "era" where we have some amazing people in the spotlight promoting selfcare and selflove and we are continuously inspiring eachother on social media, teaching and telling eachother that we <b>deserve more</b> and then a piece like this comes along and just slams all of that into the dirt. And I don't find that to be okay.</span>

    <a title="Jaye Berry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4748038-jaye-berry"><img alt="Jaye Berry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583046855p2/4748038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774807903?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaye Berry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaye Berry" href="/user/show/4748038-jaye-berry">Jaye Berry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4748038-jaye-berry?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4748038-jaye-berry?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4748038-jaye-berry?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774807903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13147141519451451623">I love reading books I KNEW would be complete garbage but gotta get them reading challenge points in.<br/><br/>Right when I thought the first book was bad?? HOW is this book even worse? I shouldn't kinkshame but screw that: y'all are messed up and need help if you actually love this series and this relationship. There is nothing redeemable about it, there are never even any cute moments. Maybe I can understand if you just like the smut but even then? It isn't even good smut! (Unless you find tampon remova</span>
  <span id="freeText13147141519451451623" style="display:none">I love reading books I KNEW would be complete garbage but gotta get them reading challenge points in.<br /><br />Right when I thought the first book was bad?? HOW is this book even worse? I shouldn't kinkshame but screw that: y'all are messed up and need help if you actually love this series and this relationship. There is nothing redeemable about it, there are never even any cute moments. Maybe I can understand if you just like the smut but even then? It isn't even good smut! (Unless you find tampon removal sexy ya nasty.) I can even understand liking it in trashy sort of car accident way but all I see is people genuinely loving this and actually WANTING #Hessa to be together?? WHY?<br /><br />If literally everything else in this book wasn't bad enough, the dialogue and writing is just so bad. People speak so weird and nothing like actual human teenagers would speak, even adults don't speak like this. I don't think I ever wanted Hardin's POV either but go off I guess. He even <i>thinks</i> like an asshole.<br /><br />For a book that is almost 700 pages, nothing ever really happens. All of this book is just every other page back and forth. They fight, they make up, they have sex, repeat repeat. It's so melodramatic and insane how much stupid drama even happens. And most of the fighting was just the same fight every single time. iT's tRuE lOvE. WHERE? A character even tells Tessa that it doesn't have to hard and awful like this but she's like, derpa derp I love him!!!1!!<br /><br />Also give me a break on the girl-on-girl hate. It is the current year and Tessa over here calling girls whores just for existing in the same space as her boyfriend. She even physically attacks a girl over that and never even feels any remorse? She's STILL mad at the other girl for having a past with Hardin and acts like she deserved to get attacked??? Molly was the ONLY one who was going to tell Tessa the truth about the gross bet but she still only blames Molly (and Steph who she was actually friends with) after she's already forgiven king douche? Fuck you Tessa.<br /><br />Otherwise Tessa is whatever as a character because we all know she is just the easy self-insert anyway but it's still sad to see her actually stand up for herself and tell this disgusting boy off... only to forgive him five seconds later. Even though Tessa is trash too, it doesn't take away from Hardin being worse trash and how this relationship is not cute. No one deserves this kind of toxic, awful situation. Abusive relationships are not romantic, or ~goals~. It is not up to women to "save" the sad bad boy. He needs professional help and he deserves to be in goddamn prison.<br /><br />This relationship has had nothing but red flags from day one and this book just waves those flags twice as hard. Hardin (hard-on? Classic) is 120% a scary abuser. It is actually insane how this book shows all the ways he is legit awful and people think it's romantic? He screams at, controls Tessa, is violent as hell to everyone and everything, and is all around a piece of shit. Aw no he's sad it's okay! Nope, he can actually CHOKE.<br /><br /><b>When a man does any of these things:</b><br />• screams at you for something you did/didn't do<br />• tells you what to do and who you can be friends with and even then he isn't happy if you have any male friends<br />• is insanely jealous to a dangerous level (LITERALLY hunts down a guy just to beat the shit out of him. Not even the first guy he's beaten up "because of you")<br />• tells you what to wear<br />• actually ends up taking control of what you're wearing anyway like tossing yoga pants because he can't stand the sight of other men looking at you<br />• he doesn't get the message about how you need space after he was shitty and 1) calls everyone you know 2) shows up at your job 3) follows you several hours away and DEMANDS you talk to him<br />• has sex with you while you're super drunk but somehow you're the one who "didn't give him a choice" ???<br />• blows every little thing out of portion like you being friends with a guy means you slept with him<br />• but if he does something shitty, it's time to manipulate you about how much he loves you and beg you to take him back (which you do but then he'll still get mad at you later and not forgive you as easy)<br />• ignores you after a fight, won't talk about things, leaves you drunk at a party to find your way home so you get a ride but he's drunk now and screams about you "bringing him to my home" when he's the jackass who left you there<br />• spends night platonically at a woman's house but when you do the same with your male friend you're a "whore"<br />• literally isolates you from everyone else because he has destroyed the relationship you had with your mother (and your only other friends were his or his stepbrother) so when you constantly fight with him and have to leave, you have nowhere to go<br />• in any sort of disagreement, he'll act like you betrayed him completely and start getting violent, throwing and breaking things, punching walls, and grabbing your wrist (don't worry though he PROMISES he will never hit you physically, even when he is blackout drunk and losing his shit. I guess emotional abuse doesn't exist in this fantasy world because his actions are just as bad as if he would just slap her.)<br />• "Get over here before I make you." "If you ever do that again..." "You don't love me anymore?" "You can't leave me, I would die without you." "YOU did this, look what I did because of you."<br /><br />I could just keep going on but honestly just read this: <a href="https://psychcentral.com/blog/21-warning-signs-of-an-emotionally-abusive-relationship/" rel="nofollow noopener">21 Warning Signs of an Emotionally Abusive Relationship</a> and you'll find EVERYTHING that happened in this book.<br /><br />Now I'm going to yeet myself off my soapbox and try to cleanse myself of this piece of shit book.</span>

<div id="review_1214950906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214950906" />
    <a title="Tanya (Girl Plus Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/416997-tanya-girl-plus-books"><img alt="Tanya (Girl Plus Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439375146p2/416997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1214950906?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya (Girl Plus Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya (Girl Plus Books)" href="/user/show/416997-tanya-girl-plus-books">Tanya (Girl Plus Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416997-tanya-girl-plus-books?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416997-tanya-girl-plus-books?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214950906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14423639854213388839">2.75 STARS<br/><br/>Like a car wreck you can't look away from... that's pretty much my relationship with this series.<br/><br/>There's not much to say about this one that I didn't say in my review of After. Probably because it felt like a rehash of the first book. Tessa and Hardin continue their insane pattern of on again-off again, I love you/I hate you, I can't live with you/I can't live without you madness. There are times when their relationship is so off the charts hideous that I wonder if I'm actually suppose</span>
  <span id="freeText14423639854213388839" style="display:none">2.75 STARS<br /><br />Like a car wreck you can't look away from... that's pretty much my relationship with this series.<br /><br />There's not much to say about this one that I didn't say in my review of After. Probably because it felt like a rehash of the first book. Tessa and Hardin continue their insane pattern of on again-off again, I love you/I hate you, I can't live with you/I can't live without you madness. There are times when their relationship is so off the charts hideous that I wonder if I'm actually supposed to be pulling for them. Because as written, these two surely do not belong together. Tessa is wishy-washy and easily swayed (despite her talk of independence) and Hardin is a d-bag to the tenth power. But I'm supposed to get behind this train wreck of a relationship and hope for their HEA? Yeah, obviously I'm missing something important. Like a shred of likability.<br /><br />I find it amusing that every guy in Tessa's life desperately wants her, loves and adores her. Noah, Hardin, Trevor, Zed. Note to Anna Todd: this does not make your protagonist likable. It does, however, make her completely unrealistic and gag-inducing.<br /><br />And I still can't figure out why anyone gives Hardin the time of day. He is rude, obnoxious, disrespectful, angry... he consistently treats everyone around him in a way that is shockingly bad and yet they all just seem to go with it. Um, why? Why doesn't anyone tell him to pack sand, take his crap attitude and get lost? Apparently I missed any passages that described his hidden charms.<br /><br />So the toxic relationship continues, the silly drama, the constant bickering and fighting and jealous rages. But, let the train wreck continue - after 1,270 pages, I refuse to give up now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14423639854213388839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2786884727" />
    <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com"><img alt="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570843185p2/70316517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️" href="/user/show/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com">Ꮗ€♫◗☿ ❤️ ilikebooksbest.com ❤️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22473458-after-we-collided">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70316517-ilikebooksbest-com?shelf=angst">angst</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2786884727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6520149858219717081"><strong>So real, so tragic, so riveting </strong><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552145052ra/27180016.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You see couples like this all the time and you think, “why does she stay with him, he makes her miserable.” They fight, they break up, they get back together and it is a viscous circle that never seems to end. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Should I ask to drive her to campus today?” <br/>I follow him down the stairs. He shakes his head at me. “What part of nonsuffocating do you not get?” <br/>“I liked you better when you kept your mouth shut.” <br/>“I liked you better when you . . . well, I never li</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText6520149858219717081" style="display:none"><strong>So real, so tragic, so riveting </strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552145052ra/27180016.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You see couples like this all the time and you think, “why does she stay with him, he makes her miserable.” They fight, they break up, they get back together and it is a viscous circle that never seems to end. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Should I ask to drive her to campus today?” <br>I follow him down the stairs. He shakes his head at me. “What part of nonsuffocating do you not get?” <br>“I liked you better when you kept your mouth shut.” <br>“I liked you better when you . . . well, I never liked you,” he says, but I can tell he’s teasing.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>I am fascinated with Hardin and Tessa despite the fact that I have read basically 1200 pages of them fighting, making up and then fighting again but surprising enough, I like it and want to keep reading. Hardin is so insecure and jealous and Tessa is sometimes the same, they like to get back at each other in the most painful ways. But when they are alone, they love each other so fiercely that you can’t help but root for them.<br><br>They both have such awful backgrounds that you feel so bad for them and you really want them to grow up and work together. Anna Todd is also great at adding a last minute cliffhanger that really makes you have to immediately buy the next book. Damn her! 🤬<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1579212843ra/28790519.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.ilikebooksbest.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a>|<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/wennel" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.facebook.com/ilikebooksbest" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>|<a href="https://smile.amazon.com/gp/profile/amzn1.account.AFFE5A2BGXJQTQMCYHFC4YHV6KFQ?preview=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a>|<a href="https://www.twitter.com/wendysu020202" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>|<a href="https://www.bookbub.com/profile/1895823057" rel="nofollow noopener">BookBub</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6578337806952906533">Audiobook...read by Shane East and Elizabeth Louise<br/><br/>The drama between Hardin and Tessa continues.<br/>It’s just the type of a relationship a parent dreams of for their child. <br/>Haha!<br/><br/>What can I say. I suppose I’m losing brain cells with each next book...<br/>but I’m still hanging around taking in the rages, the passion, the lust, the lies, daily life, the profanity, the family and friends of the college-toxic-luv-couple. <br/><br/>A couple of funnies in book two - (charming scenes from bad boy Hardin):<br/>Hardin in yoga cl</span>
  <span id="freeText6578337806952906533" style="display:none">Audiobook...read by Shane East and Elizabeth Louise<br /><br />The drama between Hardin and Tessa continues.<br />It’s just the type of a relationship a parent dreams of for their child. <br />Haha!<br /><br />What can I say. I suppose I’m losing brain cells with each next book...<br />but I’m still hanging around taking in the rages, the passion, the lust, the lies, daily life, the profanity, the family and friends of the college-toxic-luv-couple. <br /><br />A couple of funnies in book two - (charming scenes from bad boy Hardin):<br />Hardin in yoga class..,<br />Hardin ice skating...<br />Hardin babysitting a 5 year old boy named Smith... and calling him a “mini-human”.<br /><br />Book 1 was better - but<br />Book 2 exposed more background details of the young lovers Traumatic Childhoods. <br />Actually - it’s my sense - that it doesn’t matter which book is which after awhile. <br />It’s simply continuous nonstop drama.... ( from book to book), like a soap opera series with crazy messy lives. <br /><br />I’ve been taking long walks recently. <br />This audiobook series is pure trashy entertainment...<br /><br />Once again — <br />don’t even ask me to explain or justify. I’m nuts and admit it...<br />But....<br />during my long walks...<br />Somehow this series is giving me time to think - connect with myself and nature - peacefully<br />and privately. <br />This ‘trashy-book-of-flaws’....is so easy to follow with it’s own problems that I find it producing in me a drug-like state of being. <br />Calm and satisfied.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5041624061932050111">Finally I’ve finished this. One would think I should just drop it without complaining about it every 2 pages but unfortunately my slight OCD doesn’t allow me to let go. Also mostly, it was I wanted to know the story before the movie came out and if I was given a chance I would have stayed till the end without reading it. <br/><br/>First of all, I do not want anyone reading this book to think THIS is what a normal relationship. No kids, relationships are much subdued and normal than this and that does not </span>
  <span id="freeText5041624061932050111" style="display:none">Finally I’ve finished this. One would think I should just drop it without complaining about it every 2 pages but unfortunately my slight OCD doesn’t allow me to let go. Also mostly, it was I wanted to know the story before the movie came out and if I was given a chance I would have stayed till the end without reading it. <br /><br />First of all, I do not want anyone reading this book to think THIS is what a normal relationship. No kids, relationships are much subdued and normal than this and that does not make it boring. People who go through relationships like this??? Now that is psychotic. That is the nicest thing I can say about it. They need therapy. Both of them. The only reason I was able to somewhat go through the first book was because I had the movie in my head. The only reason I would ever read the rest of the books will be because of the movies. Especially Jo and Hero. Them only. ONLY. But seeing the teaser and pictures, Christian and Kim and Smith are adoooorable too. I mean it’s Candice King. She’s cute and Max Ragone is such a cute Smith. <br /><br />So basically the only good thing about this series is their movies. I hope to god that they continue the movies. That is all. Will I read the other book? Sigh. Yes. When the third movie’s teaser comes out I might. If not? Nada honey. Not in my life even if you hold me at gun point. <br /><br />#TeamHessa<br /><br />Who am I kidding? I hate myself for even thinking of reading the rest -.-</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6840326125652171704">oh, man...<br/><br/>this is a mashed potato of mashing stuff LOL or whatever the fuck i wanted to say, I m not even sure...<br/><br/>Phew...<br/><br/>Ok, I will address several things here:<br/><br/>1) after the HUGE fucked up revelation we got at the end of the book 1, I would expect, since the intention is for the two main characters to find their way to each other again, that the dude would have to grovel a little bit more than being into the 28% of the book...I mean, really?! <br/>It's not just ALL about the sex, right?! It all sound l</span>
  <span id="freeText6840326125652171704" style="display:none">oh, man...<br /><br />this is a mashed potato of mashing stuff LOL or whatever the fuck i wanted to say, I m not even sure...<br /><br />Phew...<br /><br />Ok, I will address several things here:<br /><br />1) after the HUGE fucked up revelation we got at the end of the book 1, I would expect, since the intention is for the two main characters to find their way to each other again, that the dude would have to grovel a little bit more than being into the 28% of the book...I mean, really?! <br />It's not just ALL about the sex, right?! It all sound like that famous line <i>Gary Busy</i> said in the movie <b>Point break</b> : "You're young, dumb and full of cum."<br /><br />Well, I have no choice but to agree with that line considering the events in this sequel.<br /><br />2) Jeeezus...dude, you sure have ISSUES!!! Like, serious big issues...anger management and there's a shit ton for you to do...<br /><br />3) being compassionate as the heroine is trying to be here, is not really looking good for her credibility and it all somehow comes down to her being a doormat, naive fucking doormat.<br /><br />4) the characters are being portrayed through this lens of impulsive, passionate, affectionate sexual and emotionally charged relationship without them actually knowing what that REALLY means...what these characters display towards each other and towards other people surrounding them is <i>unhealthy, wild, irrational and toxic, in one word no-good</i>, which all just looks a bit cheap, immature and trashy... annoying :/<br /><br />5) I'll use the quote from the book to emphisize the general notion I got AFTER reading it:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I'm tired of the back-and-forth, too. It's so exhausting and I can't do it anymore, I really can't.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />BUT this book ends up in a cliffy, hinting a much prolongued continuation of this turmoi of fucked up! Gah...</span>

<div id="review_1090510702" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090510702" />
    <a title="Ursula Uriarte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16751097-ursula-uriarte"><img alt="Ursula Uriarte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467336518p2/16751097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090510702?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ursula Uriarte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ursula Uriarte" href="/user/show/16751097-ursula-uriarte">Ursula Uriarte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16751097-ursula-uriarte?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16751097-ursula-uriarte?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090510702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4381071672642341600">5 very angsty stars <br/><br/>I’m just going to assume that you all have read After before reading this review ;) <br/>I would be lying if I said that I didn’t absolutely hate Hardin at the end of After, I was gutted and angry and I just didn’t see how Anna would ever manage to come back and engage us again in the story after that ultimate betrayal, I felt like I needed a support group after that ending. <br/><a href='http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/tumblr_mb4ph0l93x1rziwwco1_500_zps0uwqby1b.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417142721ra/12237656.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mb4ph0l93x1rziwwco1_500_zps0uwqby1b.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>You can read my review for After <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083143923?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here</a><br/><br/>After We Collided is told from both Tessa’s and Hardin’s point of </span>
  <span id="freeText4381071672642341600" style="display:none">5 very angsty stars <br><br>I’m just going to assume that you all have read After before reading this review ;) <br>I would be lying if I said that I didn’t absolutely hate Hardin at the end of After, I was gutted and angry and I just didn’t see how Anna would ever manage to come back and engage us again in the story after that ultimate betrayal, I felt like I needed a support group after that ending. <br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/tumblr_mb4ph0l93x1rziwwco1_500_zps0uwqby1b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417142721ra/12237656.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mb4ph0l93x1rziwwco1_500_zps0uwqby1b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You can read my review for After <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083143923?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a><br><br>After We Collided is told from both Tessa’s and Hardin’s point of view and it has never been so important to have both POVs in a story as it is in this book! <br>We find Hardin and Tessa exactly were we left off in After… I started reading already convinced there was nothing Hardin could say or do that would make me forgive him for what he did, and I was more than ready to scream at Tessa if she dared take him back. Little did I know later I would be screaming at Tessa but for completely different reasons.<br><br>I’m sure I mentioned this in my review for After but I shall say it again, Anna is a genius! <br>Hardin’s POV becomes crucial because you get to see what’s going on inside his head and the devastating pain he feels, and when I say crucial I mean it! We come from hating Hardin at the end of After and then we find out even more horrible stuff he has done and at that point I felt I couldn’t go any further. <br><br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/tumblr_mpdgpfHC321sphhoko1_500_zpso50i7xjj.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417142043ra/12237579.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mpdgpfHC321sphhoko1_500_zpso50i7xjj.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>His pain though and self-loathing kept me going. <br>He is suffering a great deal and even after everything that happened there was no doubt in my heart that he loved Tessa, even as complicated and toxic as the love between them seems to be at times. He has had it really tough and losing Tessa may be more than he can handle. <br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/tumblr_n1y6v8hzea1rijbg1o1_500_zpsizhfxqve.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417144163ra/12237950.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n1y6v8hzea1rijbg1o1_500_zpsizhfxqve.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/tumblr_n3542cNeJm1rijbg1o1_500_zpsgu8wjtmx.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417144163ra/12237951.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n3542cNeJm1rijbg1o1_500_zpsgu8wjtmx.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In After We Collided you see a new side of Hardin, one that really wants to try to be a better person, I think you get a real good glimpse at how great of a guy he can really be if he can overcome his demons. <br>One thing is for sure though he is not giving up on Tessa<br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/caleb-and-hanna_zpspxnuj1zf.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417146340ra/12238565.gif" alt=" photo caleb-and-hanna_zpspxnuj1zf.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/2-1-caleb-bc-i-love-you-alecziscute_zpshwb9ntpj.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417146340ra/12238566.gif" alt=" photo 2-1-caleb-bc-i-love-you-alecziscute_zpshwb9ntpj.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But is wanting to change and be better enough though? Enough to make someone forget the bad times?<br>Sometimes a relationship is so damaged that not even the most profound love is enough. <br>Tessa was at times beyond frustrating, UGH! I felt like slapping some sense into her (I may have screamed into my Goodreads a couple of times "Cut the man some slack for the love of Christ!")<br>I don't want to give to much away but like seriously Tessa, either give the guy break or move on!<br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/frustrated-gif_zpsmmqspeyd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417146340ra/12238567.gif" alt=" photo frustrated-gif_zpsmmqspeyd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>and on the other hand, Zed! What in the?! All I'm gonna say is... <br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/giphy_zpseoc5oyod.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417146340ra/12238568.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zpseoc5oyod.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I hope you guys are not tired of the roller coaster of feels though because it doesnt get any easier, they still fight and make up more times than I can actually remember (confession time: I'm here for it!), they have so much to work on as far as trusting each other goes and not just for Tessa but for Hardin too, but there is something Landon tells Tessa that stuck with me...<br><br><b>
  <i>"Just because he can't love you the way you want him to doesn't mean he doesn't love you with everything he has."</i>
</b><br><br> Ultimately it all boils down to that. Is their love enough to forgive each other? To trust each other? To accept each others' flaws and mistakes? <br>In After We Collided Anna doesn't disappoint though, their relationship is HOT even when rocky, and addictive. It's been a long time since I've read books that have kept me up until almost sunrise because I just couldn't put it down. <br>This book didn't fail to make me feel, and that's what makes me love Anna's work so much, I truly feel despair, anger, frustration, joy with each character, because they become that real in her writing. <br><br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/2giphy_zpsz18wklmk.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417147801ra/12238805.gif" alt=" photo 2giphy_zpsz18wklmk.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And if you thought for a second that she would cut us break with the ending, well think again because I was left picking up my jaw from the ground when I reached the last line. <br>Now I'm desperately awaiting the arrival of my copy of After We Fell (the struggle is real!) <br><a href="http://s30.photobucket.com/user/Ursula_Uriarte/media/gipiihy_zpsbfpalqjl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417147801ra/12238806.gif" alt=" photo gipiihy_zpsbfpalqjl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This series is all consuming 100% fantastic angst and one my favorites this year. <br>Thanks to Gallery Books and Simon and Schuster for providing me with this review copy.</span>

  <span id="freeText488900176430998214" style="display:none">To start with I thought I was going to truly like this fan fiction.<br />I was obviously wrong.<br />This fan fiction is dreadful , from the moment you start reading the second book you know what's happening next. To sum the book up it is basically Harry being a douchbag , abusing and treating Her badly. Tessa acts dumb and she lets Harry manipulate her. <br />The main reason why girls loved these books is because of the sex and the drama. Honestly this sucks , you get tired of the back and forth "relationship" they have. From the moment Tessa realized about the bet she should quit. If she had any self respect she would've known that this thing because it ain't no relationship , harms her. THIS FAN FICTION IS TOO FICTITIOUS !!!! these things are rubbish , I dislike this so much I didn't even finish the second book because you basically know what's happening next! It's just so bad.</span>

<div id="review_1740709423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1740709423" />
    <a title="Elle&#39;s Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44344367-elle-s-book-blog"><img alt="Elle&#39;s Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601066023p2/44344367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1740709423?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle&#39;s Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle&#39;s Book Blog" href="/user/show/44344367-elle-s-book-blog">Elle&#39;s Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44344367-elle-s-book-blog?shelf=top-favorites">top-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44344367-elle-s-book-blog?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44344367-elle-s-book-blog?shelf=college-romance">college-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44344367-elle-s-book-blog?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740709423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14441779055113225127"><b> Genre: </b> New Adult + College Romance<br/><b> Series </b> The After series (must read books in order. This is book #2). <br/><br/><b> :: 5 Pretty Little Stars :: </b><br/><br/>I don't know what it is about this series but these books are completely addicting. It doesn't even seem to matter to my brain that these two (Tessa and Hardin) are like a train wreck. I simply cannot get enough and I can't stop reading. There is also SO much drama in this series. I mean honestly, the push and pull and back and forth which take up 75% of the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText14441779055113225127" style="display:none"><b> Genre: </b> New Adult + College Romance<br /><b> Series </b> The After series (must read books in order. This is book #2). <br /><br /><b> :: 5 Pretty Little Stars :: </b><br /><br />I don't know what it is about this series but these books are completely addicting. It doesn't even seem to matter to my brain that these two (Tessa and Hardin) are like a train wreck. I simply cannot get enough and I can't stop reading. There is also SO much drama in this series. I mean honestly, the push and pull and back and forth which take up 75% of the book makes me want to rip my hair out and scream yet, I cannot get enough of it. Gosh, I don't know what it is about this one. Subliminal messaging maybe LOL??? But it's just too good to stop. <br /><br />What readers can expect from this one in particular:<br />1. A lot of crying (from the characters, not you)<br />2. A lot of intentional and unintentional hurt and pain (again, from the characters)<br />3. Insecurity<br />4. Breakups<br />5. Makeups<br />6. Shady friends<br />and more.... <br /><br />If you enjoy soap operas (hehe), new adult romance with a lot of drama but with a lot of heart, and characters that you hate but love at the same time then this is your book. Please note though that you have to read this series in order. Each book in this series surrounds Tessa and Hardin's intense relationship. Also, you will either love this series or hate it. But you should decide for yourself. I honestly love it. :-) <br /><br /><b> Rating: </b> 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="14441779055113225127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ol+2IxRQ0fsSDetwKM8l99BMa8UwPywTab1cm4JMsujnyp7IL+xe/lrNoMSXmhmRsj5YhaZaFN6tHDUT1CJ07Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vvIOjQhs29PBeN+qF3kfpM8Q7PHCLXD7pPgd3o+SK5f7ZyZmM9BU1om4lB6oLCPCrWLfsVRISDZgWXRW2fztkg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer6989463783311703460">ANNA TODD (Author/Writer/Producer) is the New York Times bestselling author of the After series of books, The Spring Girls, and the recent The Brightest Stars.<br/> <br/>Always an avid reader, Todd began writing stories on her phone on Wattpad, the reading and writing multiplatform for original stories, with After becoming its most-read series with over 1.5 billion reads. <br/> <br/>The print edition of After was pub</span>
  <span id="freeText6989463783311703460" style="display:none">ANNA TODD (Author/Writer/Producer) is the New York Times bestselling author of the After series of books, The Spring Girls, and the recent The Brightest Stars.<br /> <br />Always an avid reader, Todd began writing stories on her phone on Wattpad, the reading and writing multiplatform for original stories, with After becoming its most-read series with over 1.5 billion reads. <br /> <br />The print edition of After was published in 2014 by Simon &amp; Schuster and has since been released in over 30 languages with more than 11 million copies sold worldwide. After has been a #1 bestseller across the globe including Italy, Germany, France and Spain. She has since written eight additional novels and serves as a producer and screenwriter on the upcoming film adaptation of After We Collided, the sequel to After. <br /> <br />Todd has been hailed by Cosmopolitan as “the biggest literary phenomenon of her generation.” A native of Ohio Anna, her husband and son currently live in Los Angeles.<br /> <br />Find her at AnnaTodd.com, on Twitter at @annatodd, on Instagram at @annatodd, and on Wattpad as Imaginator1D.<br /><br />Sign up for her mailing list for all the latest news: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://eepurl.com/cEm5e9">http://eepurl.com/cEm5e9</a><br />For more information on Anna Todd visit her website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.annatodd.com/">http://www.annatodd.com/</a></span>
